The act of killing a chivalrous journalist weighed heavily on both shoulders.　Sin - a burden that can never be discarded or entrusted to someone else.

生き続ける限りそれは積み重ねられ続ける。だからこそ人は正しく生きて少しでも荷を減らすのだ。　が、この俺はあたかも精神の剛力を誇示するが如く、殺人という最大の罪を次から次へと抱え込んでいる。
As long as we continue to live, it will continue to accumulate. That's why people should live right and reduce their burden as much as possible.　But here I am, as if to show off my mental fortitude, carrying the biggest sins of murder one after another.

The two tsurugi finally completed, the first and second Muramasa, were of course the pinnacle of performance, but they also had an unusual quality.　It was only Senko Muramasa, and he had two.

一つは〝善悪相殺〟の戒 Ritsuである。　対敵を一人殺したなら味方も一人。悪しき者を一人殺したなら善き者も一人。憎む者を一人殺したなら、愛する者もまた一人、殺さねばならない。
The first is the precept of "canceling out good and evil".　If you kill one opponent, you kill one friend. If you kill one evil person, you kill one good person. If you kill one person you hate, you must also kill one person you love.

村正と結縁した mushaはこの掟を背負う。　己の善のみ盲信し、敵の善は悪と看做して排除する、その〝独善〟を力で押し通すことを、村正という tsurugiは許さないのだ。
The musha who are united with Muramasa are bound by this rule.　The tsurugi called Muramasa will not allow you to push through your "self-righteousness" by force, blindly believing only in your own goodness and dismissing the goodness of your enemies as evil.

衆に卓抜する村正の暴威で望みを遂げようとすれば、己の手でその望みを打ち砕く結末に至る。　村正 mushaは最強にして、誰よりも武力の行使を自重する人物にならざるを得ないであろう。
If you try to accomplish what you want with the might of Muramasa, who is outstanding among the people, you will end up shattering that hope with your own hands.　Muramasa musha will have to be the strongest, but the one who will be the most restrained in the use of force.

もう一つは〝精神同調〟の能である。　村正は『波』を放散し、周囲の人間の精神に仕手のそれを重ねることができるのだ。
The other is the ability to "sync" with the spirit.　Muramasa can emit "waves" and superimpose his own spirit on that of the people around him.

仕手の精神に浸透した善悪相殺の戒 Ritsuも写される。　一軍全体を、村正の思想に沿う集団へと変貌せしめられるのである。
The precept of offsetting good and evil that permeates the minds of the warriors is also captured in Ritsu.　The entire army can be transformed into a group that is in line with Muramasa's philosophy.

村正の仕手に利己心あらば、この〝精神同調〟能力を味方の軍に対して使おうとは思わないであろう。　敵軍に対して用い、戦意を奪おうとする筈である。
If Muramasa's attackers had any selfishness, they would not want to use this "psychic synchronization" ability against friendly forces.　He would use it against the enemy army to take away their will to fight.

しかし、だからこそ始祖村正は tsurugiを二領用意して、対立する両陣営に与えたのだ。　双方の村正 mushaが敵に対して〝精神同調〟を行使し合えば、一方だけが優勢になるような事態は起きない。
However, that is why the original Muramasa prepared two sets of tsurugi and gave them to the two opposing camps.　If both Muramasa musha exercise "mental synchronization" against the enemy, there will be no situation where only one side will have the upper hand.

戦場は遍く〝善悪相殺〟の戒 Ritsuに支配される。
The battlefield is universally dominated by the commandment Ritsu of "offsetting good and evil.

完璧――そう言って良かった。　始祖村正が tsurugiに懸けた理想は、これ以上はないという形で結実した。
I am glad to say that it was perfect.　The ideal that the founder Muramasa had put into tsurugi came to fruition in a way that could not be surpassed.

この tsurugiは必ずや世に平和をもたらす。　長きに渡り続いた南北朝の乱を、穏健に終息させる。
This tsurugi will surely bring peace to the world.　It will bring a peaceful end to the long-running conflict between the Northern and Southern dynasties.

The era of the Northern and Southern Dynasties ended with an unprecedented war of annihilation that killed an estimated 10 to 20 percent of the population of the time in just one year.

The general of the Northern Dynasty army, who was presented with the founder Muramasa, was in a situation where he could not be said to have a solid power base.　Rather than a ruler, he was more like a coordinator of interests among the generals.

政治の才に優れた実弟の力を借りて、漸う軍をまとめていたのである。　些細な情勢の変化、利害関係の変動から敵意を買い、昨日までの部下に盾突かれることも一切ではなかった。
With the help of his own brother, who had a great talent for politics, he was finally able to organize his army.　The slightest change in the situation or change of interest could cause hostility, and not a single one of his subordinates could shield him until yesterday.

村正の戒 Ritsuが持つ拘束力は絶対である。　敵を殺した彼は自分の意思によらずして刃の向きを返し、傍らに立つ味方を斬り伏せた。
The binding power of Muramasa's precepts, Ritsu, is absolute.　Having killed his enemy, he turned his blade around and cut down his ally standing beside him without his will.

公私両面で彼を支えてくれていた、最愛の弟を。
His beloved brother, who had supported him in both his public and private life.

In order to protect his allies from the "wave" of madness, the leader of the Southern Court, who was the second Muramasa, had no choice but to preemptively place the entire army under his mental influence.

かくして前例のない地獄的な闘争が地上に発現する。
Thus, an unprecedented hellish struggle will emerge on earth.

一方は、手当たり次第何もかも破壊し殺し尽くさんとする魔獣の群れ。　一方は、敵兵を一人殺す都度、肩並べて戦う友をも一人ずつ殺してゆく悲愴の軍団。
On the one hand, there is a pack of demonic beasts that want to destroy and kill everything at random.　On the other hand, a pathetic army that kills one friend for every enemy soldier it kills.

末世の相そのものであった。　この世において人間の生命は秋の田の稲穂のように、無造作に刈り取られ、三途の川の向こうへ流された。
It was the phase of the last days itself.　In this world, human life is like the ears of rice in the autumn fields, carelessly harvested and swept away to the other side of the Sanzu River.

どれほどの人が死に、どれほどの村が滅んだか……　正確に知る者など誰もいない。知ろうとする意欲を持つ者もいなかったろう。
No one knew exactly how many people died and how many villages were destroyed. ...... No one had the desire to know. No one would have had the motivation to find out.

乱の最中、人々はただ生き延びるために必死であり、乱が果てた後は、世間の惨状にただ呆然とするばかりであった。
During the rebellion, people were just struggling to survive, and after it was over, they were just stunned by the devastation of the world.

神懸かりの力を揮った始祖村正と北朝主将に南朝の将とその麾下十三 craftが挑み、遂にこれを討ち果たして乱の源を断った時――曰く「いまや大和では人よりも、死肉を食らう犬猫の方が栄えている」……。
When the southern dynasty generals and their 13 troops challenged the founder Muramasa and the northern dynasty generals, who displayed divine power, and finally defeated them and cut off the source of the rebellion - "Now in Yamato, dogs and cats that eat dead flesh are more prosperous than people." ......

ある法師の嘆弁である。
This is the lament of a Buddhist priest.

He asked me to accept my will.　I returned a complete rejection to the tailor who wanted only to ...... admit that he was willing to fight and take responsibility for his own will.

彼は私の意志を認めると言ってくれたのに。　あの錆びた錠前のような頑固者が。なのに。　　けれどどうしても、それは認められないのだ。
Even though he said he would grant me my will.　He was as stubborn as a rusty lock. And yet.　　But for the life of me, I can't admit it.

Just as he saw my past during the engagement with Aoe, I saw his old days.　So I know.

彼は本来、小さな町で穏やかに暮らす人間であったことを。　その生活を奪ったのが、私と先代――二領の村正だということを。
He was originally a man who lived peacefully in a small town.　It was me and my predecessor, the second Muramasa, who took that life away from him.

村正の存在さえなかったなら、彼は平穏な日々を命尽きるまで続けられたのだ。　……五百年前、私が愚かなことを願わなければ！
If only Muramasa hadn't existed, he could have continued his days in peace until the end of his life.　...... five hundred years ago, if I had not foolishly wished!

これを取り除くなら、鍛造行程をすべて見直さなくてはならない。　祖父と母、そして祖母と父。一門の探究の総決算であるそれを、独力で一から立て直さねばならないのだ。

（無明）
(indistinct)

吉野御流の理を、胸中に落とし込む。
I let the logic of the Yoshino Goryu fall into my heart.

武道一般には『先を取る』という表現で語られる事が多い。　勝機勝法を意味する言葉としては後の先が著名だが、これはそれに対応するものだ。
In martial arts in general, it is often referred to as 'taking the first step'.　This is the counterpart to the more prominent term later on, which refers to a winning strategy.

後の先が敵に先手を打たせ、これを防いで勝を取る理念であるのに対し、　先は敵が先手を打とうとする瞬間を制して勝利する。
The first step is to prevent the enemy from making the first move and win the game, while the second step is to win the game by controlling the moment when the enemy tries to make the first move.

攻撃を仕掛けに出る瞬間とは、無防備なものである。　誰しも攻撃を行う時にはまず攻撃の意思を起こさねばならず、攻撃の意思を起こせば防御への意識が散るからである。
The moment you go out to attack is the moment when you are defenseless.　This is because everyone must first generate the intention to attack, and once the intention to attack is generated, the consciousness of defense is scattered.

先の機を確実に捉えられたなら、勝利は約束されたも同然だ。　　しかし、それが容易ならぬのは当然であった。
If we could seize the opportunity ahead of us, victory would be as good as assured.　　However, it was obvious that this would not be easy.

先の勝機の訪れは、目に見えてわかるものではない。　あくまでも敵の内面、心の中の動きなのだから。
It is not something that you can visibly tell when you are about to win.　It is only the inner workings of the enemy's mind.

しかも、時間的に極めて短い。　攻撃を掛けると決めてから実際に殴るまで、三秒も必要とする人間はいないだろう。精々が一秒。練達の武人なら一瞬未満に抑えて当たり前である。
Moreover, the time frame is extremely short.　No one needs more than three seconds from the moment they decide to attack to the moment they actually hit. One second at most. If you're a skilled warrior, it's natural to keep it to less than a second.

視覚で認識できない変化を、極少の時間で察知し、そして敵よりも早く動かねばならない。　気の遠くなる難業と云うべきであった。
They had to detect changes that could not be detected visually, in a very short time, and move faster than the enemy.　It was a daunting and difficult task.

吉野御流はこの難業を、無明の理と称して修練者に求める。　　――闇夜ニ在テ道ヲ拓ク。
The Yoshino Goryu calls this difficult task the "truth of the blind" and asks the practitioner to　　--The Yoshino Goryu asks the practitioner to find the way in the dark of night.

そしてこの理は、突き詰めた果て、更に上位の理へ至るものとする。　　――無想。
And this truth, when pushed to the limit, shall lead to a higher truth.　　--No thought.

それは最早、先の機を狙ってどうの、後の先を取るためにどうの、という領域を超えた世界である。　想が無しの語義通り、まずそうした考えを持たない。
